As well as celebrating the achievements of armed forces veterans, Brown\'s speech at the first event for the celebration said: </p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Scots and people from the rest of the UK share the purpose that Britain has something to say to the rest of the world about the values of freedom, democracy and the dignity of the people that you stand up for. So at a time when people can talk about football and devolution and money, it is important that we also remember the values that we share in common.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">Geographic distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_diaspora" title="British diaspora">British diaspora</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_British_immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by British immigrants">List of countries by British immigrants</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_diaspora_by_country.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/British_diaspora_by_country.svg/220px-British_diaspora_by_country.svg.png" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/British_diaspora_by_country.svg/330px-British_diaspora_by_country.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/British_diaspora_by_country.svg/440px-British_diaspora_by_country.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2499" data-file-height="1062" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_diaspora_by_country.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A world map showing the distribution of people by self-reported British ancestral or ethnic diaspora.<br /> <b>Legend:</b> <div>  &#32; <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00112B; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Greater than 55%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #002255; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;50-55%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #003380; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;45-50%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0044aa; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;40-45%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0055d4; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;35-40%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0066ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;30-35%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #2a7fff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;25-30%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5599ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;20-25%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #80b3ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;15-20%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aaccff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;10-15%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #e0e0e0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Less than 10%</div> &#32; </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The earliest migrations of Britons date from the 5th and 6th centuries AD, when Brittonic Celts fleeing the Anglo-Saxon invasions migrated what is today northern France and north western Spain and forged the colonies of <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Britonia" title="Britonia">Britonia</a>. Brittany remained independent of France until the early 16th century and still retains a distinct Brittonic culture and language, whilst Britonia in modern <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> was absorbed into Spanish states by the end of the 9th century AD.\n</p><p>Britons - people with British citizenship or of British descent - have a significant presence in a number of countries other than the United Kingdom, and in particular in those with historic connections to the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> the British were one of the earliest and largest communities to emigrate out of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and the British Empire\'s expansion during the first half of the 19th century triggered an "extraordinary dispersion of the British people", resulting in particular concentrations "in <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis47_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis47-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British Empire was "built on waves of migration overseas by British people",<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh254_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh254-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> who left the United Kingdom and "reached across the globe and permanently affected population structures in three continents".<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis47_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis47-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> As a result of the <a href="/wiki/British_colonisation_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="British colonisation of the Americas">British colonisation of the Americas</a>, what became the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> was "easily the greatest single destination of emigrant British", but in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> the British experienced a <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> higher than "anything seen before" resulting in the displacement of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">indigenous Australians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis47_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis47-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In colonies such as <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Southern Rhodesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_East_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="British East Africa">British East Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, permanently resident British communities were established and whilst never more than a numerical minority these Britons "exercised a dominant influence" upon the culture and politics of those lands.<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh254_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh254-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In Australia, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> "people of British origin came to constitute the majority of the population" contributing to these states becoming integral to the <a href="/wiki/Anglosphere" title="Anglosphere">Anglosphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh254_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh254-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_1861" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 1861">United Kingdom Census 1861</a> estimated the size of the overseas British to be around 2.5 million, but concluded that most of these were "not conventional settlers" but rather "travellers, merchants, professionals, and military personnel".<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis47_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis47-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> By 1890, there were over 1.5 million further UK-born people living in Australia, Canada, New Zealand and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis47_50-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis47-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> A 2006 publication from the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Public_Policy_Research" title="Institute for Public Policy Research">Institute for Public Policy Research</a> estimated 5.6 million Britons lived outside of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-BritsAbroad_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritsAbroad-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Outside of the United Kingdom and its <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">Overseas Territories</a>, the largest proportions of people of self-identified <a href="/wiki/British_diaspora" title="British diaspora">ethnic British descent</a> in the world are found in New Zealand (58%),<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Australia (43%)<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> and Canada (32%),<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> followed by a considerably smaller minority in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (12%).<sup id="cite_ref-auto_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Hong Kong has the highest proportion of British citizens outside of the United Kingdom and its Overseas Territories, with 47% of Hong Kong residents holding a British National (Overseas) citizenship or a British citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet" title="First Fleet">First Fleet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Celtic_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Celtic Australian">Anglo-Celtic Australian</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Australia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/220px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/330px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/440px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Australia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Australia" title="Flag of Australia">flag of Australia</a> was approved by Australian and British authorities, and features a <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a>\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Flag of the United Kingdom">flag of the United Kingdom</a>\xe2\x80\x94in the canton. Australia has one of the largest concentrations of people of British heritage.</div></div></div>\n<p>From the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia_(1788%E2%80%931850)" title="History of Australia (1788\xe2\x80\x931850)">beginning of Australia\'s colonial period</a> until after the Second World War, people from the United Kingdom made up a large majority of people coming to Australia, meaning that many people born in Australia can trace their origins to Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-ausbrit_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ausbrit-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The colony of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, founded on 26 January 1788, was part of the eastern half of Australia claimed by the Kingdom of Great Britain in 1770, and initially settled by Britons through <a href="/wiki/Penal_transportation" title="Penal transportation">penal transportation</a>. Together with another five largely self-governing Crown Colonies, the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">federation of Australia</a> was achieved on 1 January 1901.\n</p><p>Its history of British dominance meant that Australia was "grounded in British culture and political traditions that had been transported to the Australian colonies in the nineteenth century and become part of colonial culture and politics".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalligan_et_al._2001113_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalligan_et_al._2001113-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Australia maintains the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a> of Parliamentary Government and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Australia">Queen of Australia</a>. Until 1987, the national status of Australian citizens was formally described as "British Subject: Citizen of Australia". Britons continue to make up a substantial proportion of immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-ausbrit_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ausbrit-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">6 states of Australia</a> retain the flag of the United Kingdom in the canton of their respective flags.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_overseas_territories">British overseas territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: British overseas territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>\nThe approximately 250,000 people of the <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territories">British overseas territories</a> are British by <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a>, via origins or <a href="/wiki/Naturalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Naturalisation">naturalisation</a>. Along with aspects of common British identity, each of them has their own distinct identity shaped in the respective particular circumstances of political, economic, ethnic, social and cultural history. For instance, in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islanders" title="Falkland Islanders">Falkland Islanders</a>, Lewis Clifton the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_(politics)" title="Speaker (politics)">Speaker</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_the_Falkland_Islands" title="Legislative Council of the Falkland Islands">Legislative Council of the Falkland Islands</a>, explains: </p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>British cultural, economic, social, political and educational values create a unique British-like, Falkland Islands. Yet Islanders feel distinctly different from their fellow citizens who reside in the United Kingdom. This might have something to do with geographical isolation or with living on a smaller island\xe2\x80\x94perhaps akin to those Britons not feeling European.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> \n</p></blockquote>\n<p>In contrast, for the majority of the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarians" title="Gibraltarians">Gibraltarians</a>, who live in <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, there is an "insistence on their Britishness" which "carries excessive loyalty" to Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-inde_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inde-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The sovereignty of Gibraltar has been a point of contention in <a href="/wiki/Spain%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Spain\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom relations">Spain\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom relations</a>, but an overwhelming number of Gibraltarians embrace Britishness with strong conviction, in direct opposition to <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">Spanish territorial claims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-inde_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inde-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg/220px-VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg/330px-VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg/440px-VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="757" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VE_Day_celebrations_on_Bay_Street_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">V-E Day</a> celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, May 1945</div></div></div>\n<p>Canada traces its statehood to the <a href="/wiki/French_colonisation_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="French colonisation of the Americas">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_colonisation_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="British colonisation of the Americas">English and Scottish</a> expeditions of North America from the late-15th century. France ceded nearly all of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> in 1763 after the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years\' War</a>, and so after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a> in 1776, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Quebec_(1763%E2%80%931791)" title="Province of Quebec (1763\xe2\x80\x931791)">Quebec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> formed "the nucleus of the colonies that constituted Britain\'s remaining stake on the North American continent".<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh34_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh34-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> attracted the <a href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalist" title="United Empire Loyalist">United Empire Loyalists</a>, Britons who migrated out of what they considered the "rebellious" <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, increasing the size of British communities in what was to become Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Marsh34_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marsh34-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg/170px-TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg" width="170" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg/255px-TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg/340px-TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg 2x" data-file-width="411" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TimbrePosteCanada5centsElizabethIIWilding1954.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Postage stamp with portrait of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, 1954</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1867 there was a union of three colonies with British North America which together formed the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> This began an <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Canada" title="Territorial evolution of Canada">accretion of additional provinces and territories</a> and a process of increasing autonomy from the United Kingdom, highlighted by the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a> and culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Act_1982" title="Canada Act 1982">Canada Act 1982</a>, which severed the vestiges of legal dependence on the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">parliament of the United Kingdom</a>. Nevertheless, it is recognised that there is a "continuing importance of Canada\'s long and close relationship with Britain";<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> large parts of Canada\'s modern population claim "British origins" and the cultural impact of the British upon Canada\'s institutions is profound.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was not until 1977 that the phrase "A Canadian citizen is a British subject" ceased to be used in Canadian passports. The <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Canada" title="Politics of Canada">politics of Canada</a> are strongly influenced by British political culture.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MacLeod17_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacLeod17-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Although significant modifications have been made, Canada is governed by a democratic parliamentary framework comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>, and retains <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">The Queen of Canada</a> and Head of State.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Buck1_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buck1-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> English is the mostly commonly spoken language used in Canada and it is an official language of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>British iconography remains present in the design of many <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_flags" title="List of Canadian flags">Canadian flags</a>, with 10 out of 13 Canadian provincial and territorial flags adopting some form of British symbolism in their design. The flag of the United Kingdom is also an official ceremonial flag in Canada known as the Royal Union Flag which is flown outside of federal buildings three days of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-DCH_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCH-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ruf_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ruf-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_European" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand European">New Zealand European</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_New_Zealand" title="Immigration to New Zealand">Immigration to New Zealand</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/220px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/330px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/440px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_New_Zealand" title="Flag of New Zealand">flag of New Zealand</a> features a <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a>\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Flag of the United Kingdom">flag of the United Kingdom</a>\xe2\x80\x94in the canton. <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_flag_referendums,_2015-16" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand flag referendums, 2015-16">A referendum held in 2016</a> found that 57% of New Zealand voters wanted to retain the current design of the New Zealand flag.</div></div></div>\n<p>A long-term result of <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>\'s voyage of 1768\xe2\x80\x931771,<sup id="cite_ref-MeinSmith23_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeinSmith23-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> a significant number of New Zealanders are of British descent, for whom a sense of Britishness has contributed to their identity.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> As late as the 1950s, it was common for British New Zealanders to refer to themselves as British, such as when Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Keith_Holyoake" title="Keith Holyoake">Keith Holyoake</a> described Sir <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Hillary" title="Edmund Hillary">Edmund Hillary</a>\'s successful ascent of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a> as putting "the British race and New Zealand on top of the world".<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_passport" title="New Zealand passport">New Zealand passports</a> described nationals as "British Subject: Citizen of New Zealand" until 1974, when this was changed to "New Zealand citizen".<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an interview with the <i><a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Listener" title="New Zealand Listener">New Zealand Listener</a></i> in 2006, <a href="/wiki/Don_Brash" title="Don Brash">Don Brash</a>, the then <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(New_Zealand)" title="Leader of the Opposition (New Zealand)">Leader of the Opposition</a>, said:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>British immigrants fit in here very well. My own ancestry is all British. New Zealand values are British values, derived from centuries of struggle since Magna Carta. Those things make New Zealand the society it is.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_New_Zealand" title="Politics of New Zealand">politics of New Zealand</a> are strongly influenced by British political culture. Although significant modifications have been made, New Zealand is governed by a democratic parliamentary framework comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>, and retains <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as the head of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_New_Zealand" title="Monarchy of New Zealand">monarchy of New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> English is the dominant official language used in New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law_and_Hong_Kong" title="British nationality law and Hong Kong">British nationality law and Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_National_(Overseas)" title="British National (Overseas)">British National (Overseas)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britons_in_Hong_Kong" title="Britons in Hong Kong">Britons in Hong Kong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Handover" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong Handover">Hong Kong Handover</a></div><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(November 2012)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>British nationality law as it pertains to <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> has been unusual ever since Hong Kong became a <a href="/wiki/British_colony" class="mw-redirect" title="British colony">British colony</a> in 1842. From its beginning as a sparsely populated trading port to its modern role as a cosmopolitan international financial centre of over seven million people, the territory has attracted refugees, immigrants and expatriates alike searching for a new life.\nCitizenship matters were complicated by the fact that <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">British nationality law</a> treated those born in Hong Kong as <a href="/wiki/British_subjects" class="mw-redirect" title="British subjects">British subjects</a> (although they did not enjoy full rights and citizenship), while the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a> (PRC) did not recognise Hong Kong Chinese as such. The main reason for this was that recognising these people as British was seen as a tacit acceptance of a series of historical treaties that the PRC labelled as "unequal", including the ones which ceded <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kowloon_Peninsula" title="Kowloon Peninsula">Kowloon Peninsula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_Territories" title="New Territories">New Territories</a> to Britain. The British government, however, recognising the unique political situation of Hong Kong, granted 3.4 million Hong Kongers a new type of nationality known as <a href="/wiki/British_National_(Overseas)" title="British National (Overseas)">British National (Overseas)</a>, which is established in accordance with the Hong Kong Act 1985. Among those 3.4 million people, there are many British Nationals (Overseas) who are eligible for full British citizenship. Both British Nationals (Overseas) and British citizens are British nationals and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_citizen" title="Commonwealth citizen">Commonwealth citizens</a> according to the British Nationality Law, which enables them to various rights in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/British_American" class="mw-redirect" title="British American">British American</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/British_colonisation_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="British colonisation of the Americas">British colonisation of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a></div>\n<p>An English presence in North America began with the <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Roanoke Colony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a> in the late-16th century, but the first successful English settlement was established in 1607, on the <a href="/wiki/James_River_(Virginia)" class="mw-redirect" title="James River (Virginia)">James River</a> at <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown</a>. By the 1610s an estimated 1,300 English people had travelled to North America, the "first of many millions from the British Isles".<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis48_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis48-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In 1620 the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_(Plymouth_Colony)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim (Plymouth Colony)">Pilgrims</a> established the English imperial venture of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a>, beginning "a remarkable acceleration of permanent emigration from England" with over 60% of trans-Atlantic English migrants settling in the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Colonies" title="New England Colonies">New England Colonies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis48_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis48-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> During the 17th century an estimated 350,000 English and Welsh migrants arrived in North America, which in the century after the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a> was surpassed in rate and number by Scottish and Irish migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-BritDis49_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BritDis49-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British policy of <a href="/wiki/Salutary_neglect" title="Salutary neglect">salutary neglect</a> for its North American colonies intended to minimise trade restrictions as a way of ensuring they stayed loyal to British interests.<sup id="cite_ref-history_of_colonial_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history_of_colonial-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> This permitted the development of the <a href="/wiki/American_Dream" title="American Dream">American Dream</a>, a cultural spirit distinct from that of its European founders.<sup id="cite_ref-history_of_colonial_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history_of_colonial-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a> began an armed rebellion against British rule in 1775 when they rejected the <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_Englishmen" title="Rights of Englishmen">right</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Great_Britain" title="Parliament of Great Britain">Parliament of Great Britain</a> to govern them <a href="/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation" title="No taxation without representation">without representation</a>; they proclaimed their independence in 1776, and constituted the first thirteen states of the United States of America, which became a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in 1781 with the ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">Articles of Confederation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">1783 Treaty of Paris</a> represented Great Britain\'s formal acknowledgement of the United States\' sovereignty at the end of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-road_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-road-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nevertheless, longstanding cultural and historical ties have, in more modern times, resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Special_Relationship" title="Special Relationship">Special Relationship</a>, the historically close political, diplomatic, and military co-operation between the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_%E2%80%93_United_States_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom \xe2\x80\x93 United States relations">United Kingdom and United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wither_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wither-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Linda_Colley" title="Linda Colley">Linda Colley</a>, a professor of history at <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> and specialist in Britishness, suggested that because of their colonial influence on the United States, the British find Americans a "mysterious and paradoxical people, physically distant but culturally close, engagingly similar yet irritatingly different".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest concentrations of self-reported British ethnic ancestry in the United States were found to be in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> (35%), <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> (30%), <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> (25%) and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> (25%) at the 2016 United States Census.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Chilean" title="British Chilean">British Chilean</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antofagasta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Antofagasta.jpg/220px-Antofagasta.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Antofagasta.jpg/330px-Antofagasta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Antofagasta.jpg/440px-Antofagasta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antofagasta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British and Chilean flags in a monument in <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta" title="Antofagasta">Antofagasta</a> city</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg/100px-Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg.png" width="100" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg/150px-Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg/200px-Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="711" data-file-height="1089" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Escudo_de_Coquimbo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coat of arms of <a href="/wiki/Coquimbo" title="Coquimbo">Coquimbo</a>, with the Union Flag.</div></div></div>\n<p>Approximately 4% of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile\'s</a> population is of British or Irish descent.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Over 50,000<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> British <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Chile" title="Immigration to Chile">immigrants settled in Chile</a> from 1840 to 1914. A significant number of them settled in <a href="/wiki/Magallanes_Province" title="Magallanes Province">Magallanes Province</a>, especially in the city of <a href="/wiki/Punta_Arenas,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Punta Arenas, Chile">Punta Arenas</a> when it flourished as a major global seaport for ships crossing between the Atlantic and Pacific Oceans through the Strait of Magellan. Around 32,000 English settled in <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valpara\xc3\xadso">Valpara\xc3\xadso</a>, influencing the port city to the extent of making it virtually a British colony during the last decades of the 19th century and the beginning of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-galeon_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-galeon-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> However, the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> in 1914 and the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> drove many of them away from the city or back to Europe.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valpara\xc3\xadso">Valpara\xc3\xadso</a>, they created their largest and most important colony, bringing with them neighbourhoods of British character, schools, <a href="/wiki/Social_clubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Social clubs">social clubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sports_clubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports clubs">sports clubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_organisations" class="mw-redirect" title="Business organisations">business organisations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Periodicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Periodicals">periodicals</a>. Even today their influence is apparent in specific areas, such as the banks and the navy, as well as in certain social activities, such as <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, horse racing, and the custom of drinking tea.\n</p><p>During the movement for <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> (1818), it was mainly the British who formed the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Navy" title="Chilean Navy">Chilean Navy</a>, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cochrane,_10th_Earl_of_Dundonald" title="Thomas Cochrane, 10th Earl of Dundonald">Lord Cochrane</a>.\n</p><p>British investment helped Chile become prosperous and British seamen helped the Chilean navy become a strong force in the South Pacific. Chile won two wars, the first against the Peru-Bolivian Confederation and the second, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a>, in 1878\xe2\x80\x9379, against an alliance between <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>. The liberal-socialist "Revolution of 1891" introduced political reforms modelled on British parliamentary practice and lawmaking.\n</p><p>British immigrants were also important in the northern zone of the country during the <a href="/wiki/Saltpetre" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltpetre">saltpetre</a> boom, in the ports of <a href="/wiki/Iquique" title="Iquique">Iquique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pisagua,_Chile" title="Pisagua, Chile">Pisagua</a>. The "King of Saltpetre", <a href="/wiki/John_Thomas_North" title="John Thomas North">John Thomas North</a>, was the principal tycoon of nitrate mining. The British legacy is reflected in the streets of the historic district of the city of Iquique, with the foundation of various institutions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Club_Hipico_de_Santiago" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Hipico de Santiago">Club H\xc3\xadpico</a> (Racing Club). Nevertheless, the British active presence came to an end with the saltpetre crisis during the 1930s.\n</p><p>Some <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scots</a> settled in the country\'s more temperate regions, where the climate and the forested landscape with glaciers and islands may have reminded them of their homeland (the Highlands and Northern Scotland) while <a href="/wiki/English_Chilean" class="mw-redirect" title="English Chilean">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Chilean" title="Welsh Chilean">Welsh</a> made up the rest. The Irish immigrants, who were frequently confused with the British, arrived as <a href="/wiki/Merchants" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchants">merchants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tradesmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Tradesmen">tradesmen</a> and sailors, settling along with the British in the main trading cities and ports.\n</p><p>An important contingent of British (principally Welsh) immigrants arrived between 1914 and 1950, settling in the present-day region of <a href="/wiki/Magallanes_y_la_Ant%C3%A1rtica_Chilena_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Magallanes y la Ant\xc3\xa1rtica Chilena Region">Magallanes</a>. British families were established in other areas of the country, such as <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coquimbo" title="Coquimbo">Coquimbo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Araucan%C3%ADa_Region" title="Araucan\xc3\xada Region">Araucan\xc3\xada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chilo%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Chilo\xc3\xa9">Chilo\xc3\xa9</a>.\n</p><p>The cultural legacy of the British in Chile is notable and has spread beyond the British Chilean community into society at large. Customs taken from the British include <a href="/wiki/Afternoon_tea" class="mw-redirect" title="Afternoon tea">afternoon tea</a> (called <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">onces</a> by Chileans), <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a>. Another legacy is the widespread use of British personal names by Chileans.\n</p><p>Chile has the largest population of descendants of British settlers in Latin America. Over 700,000 Chileans may have British (English, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a>) origin, amounting to 4.5% of Chile\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-british_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-british-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/British_diaspora_in_Africa" title="British diaspora in Africa">British diaspora in Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/1820_Settlers" title="1820 Settlers">1820 Settlers</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/White_South_Africans" title="White South Africans">White South Africans</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(January 2013)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg/170px-Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg/255px-Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg/340px-Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="903" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cecil_Rhodes_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cecil_Rhodes" title="Cecil Rhodes">Cecil John Rhodes</a>, the 6th <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Cape_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of the Cape Colony">Prime Minister of the Cape Colony</a> (divided between two provinces in modern-day South Africa) and founder of the <a href="/wiki/De_Beers" title="De Beers">De Beers</a> diamond company.</div></div></div>\n<p>The British arrived in the area which would become the modern-day <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> during the early 18th century, yet substantial settlement only started end of the 18th century, in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>; the British first explored the area for conquests for or related to the Slave Trade. In the late 19th century, the discovery of gold and diamonds further encouraged colonisation of South Africa by the British, and the population of the British-South Africans rose substantially, although there was fierce rivalry between the British and <a href="/wiki/Afrikaners" title="Afrikaners">Afrikaners</a> (descendants of Dutch colonists) in the period known as the <a href="/wiki/Boer_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Boer Wars">Boer Wars</a>. When apartheid first started most British-South Africans were mostly keen on keeping and even strengthening its ties with the United Kingdom. The latest census in South Africa showed that there are almost 2 million British-South Africans; they make up about 40% of the total <a href="/wiki/White_South_African" class="mw-redirect" title="White South African">White South African</a> demographic, and the greatest white British ancestry populations in South Africa are in the <a href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Natal" title="KwaZulu-Natal">KwaZulu-Natal</a> province and in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Plantations_of_Ireland" title="Plantations of Ireland">Plantations of Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">Unionism in Ireland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg/220px-The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg" width="220" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg/330px-The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg/440px-The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Special_Air_Service_during_the_Second_World_War_MH24415.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paddy_Mayne" title="Paddy Mayne">Paddy Mayne</a> from <a href="/wiki/County_Down" title="County Down">County Down</a>; a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Special_Air_Service" title="Special Air Service">SAS</a>; was one of the most decorated British soldiers of World War II. He also played rugby for Ireland.</div></div></div>\n<p>Plantations of Ireland introduced large numbers of people from Great Britain to <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> throughout the Middle Ages and <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Ascendancy" title="Protestant Ascendancy">Protestant Ascendancy</a>, the aristocratic class of the <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Ireland" title="Lordship of Ireland">Lordship of Ireland</a>, broadly identified themselves as <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In the sixteenth and seventeenth centuries, Protestant British settlers subjugated Catholic, Gaelic inhabitants in the north of Ireland during the <a href="/wiki/Plantation_of_Ulster" title="Plantation of Ulster">Plantation of Ulster</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Williamite_War_in_Ireland" title="Williamite War in Ireland">Williamite War in Ireland</a>; it was "an explicit attempt to control Ireland strategically by introducing ethnic and religious elements loyal to the British interest in Ireland".<sup id="cite_ref-Craith169_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Craith169-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_people" title="Ulster Scots people">Ulster Scots people</a> are an ethnic group of British origin in Ireland, broadly descended from <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Lowlands" title="Scottish Lowlands">Lowland Scots</a> who settled in large numbers in the Province of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> during the planned process of <a href="/wiki/Colonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation">colonisations</a> of Ireland which took place in the reign of James VI of Scotland and I of England. Together with English and Welsh settlers, these Scots introduced Protestantism (particularly the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterianism</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots</a> and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English languages</a> to, mainly, northeastern Ireland. With the partition of Ireland and independence for what is now the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> some of these people found themselves no longer living within the United Kingdom.\n</p><p>Northern Ireland itself was, for many years, the site of a violent and bitter ethno-sectarian conflict\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a>\xe2\x80\x94between those claiming to represent <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">Irish nationalism</a>, who are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, and those claiming to represent <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">British unionism</a>, who are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Unionists want Northern Ireland to remain part of the United Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> while nationalists desire a <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">united Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998, most of the paramilitary groups involved in the Troubles have ceased their armed campaigns, and constitutionally, the <a href="/wiki/People_of_Northern_Ireland" title="People of Northern Ireland">people of Northern Ireland</a> have been recognised as "all persons born in Northern Ireland and having, at the time of their birth, at least one parent who is a British citizen, an Irish citizen or is otherwise entitled to reside in Northern Ireland without any restriction on their period of residence".<sup id="cite_ref-GFA_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFA-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The Good Friday Agreement guarantees the "recognition of the birthright of all the people of Northern Ireland to identify themselves and be accepted as Irish or British, or both, as they may so choose".<sup id="cite_ref-GFA_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFA-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">Culture of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>Result from the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, British cultural influence can be observed in the language and culture of a geographically wide assortment of countries such as <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territories</a>. These states are sometimes collectively known as the <a href="/wiki/Anglosphere" title="Anglosphere">Anglosphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBennett200580_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBennett200580-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> As well as the British influence on its empire, the empire also influenced British culture, particularly <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British cuisine</a>. Innovations and movements within the wider-<a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">culture of Europe</a> have also changed the United Kingdom; <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">Humanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> have developed from broader <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>.\n</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_formation_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="History of the formation of the United Kingdom">history of the formation of the United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_England" title="Culture of England">cultures of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Scotland" title="Culture of Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Wales" title="Culture of Wales">Wales</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Culture of Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> are diverse and have varying degrees of overlap and distinctiveness.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fish_and_chips.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Fish_and_chips.jpg/220px-Fish_and_chips.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Fish_and_chips.jpg/330px-Fish_and_chips.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Fish_and_chips.jpg/440px-Fish_and_chips.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1152" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fish_and_chips.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fish_and_chips" title="Fish and chips">Fish and chips</a>, a popular <a href="/wiki/Take-away_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Take-away food">take-away food</a> throughout the United Kingdom, has been described as the quintessential British dish.<sup id="cite_ref-Walton_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walton-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Historically, <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British cuisine</a> has meant "unfussy dishes made with quality local ingredients, matched with simple sauces to accentuate flavour, rather than disguise it".<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> It has been "vilified as unimaginative and heavy", and traditionally been limited in its international recognition to the <a href="/wiki/Full_breakfast" title="Full breakfast">full breakfast</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Christmas_dinner" title="Christmas dinner">Christmas dinner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Spencer_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spencer-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> This is despite British cuisine having absorbed the culinary influences of those who have <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_Kingdom_since_1922" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration to the United Kingdom since 1922">settled in Britain</a>, resulting in hybrid dishes such as the <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">British Asian</a> <a href="/wiki/Chicken_tikka_masala" title="Chicken tikka masala">Chicken tikka masala</a>, hailed by some as "Britain\'s true national dish".<sup id="cite_ref-bbcenc_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcenc-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Celtic_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic fields">Celtic agriculture</a> and animal breeding produced a wide variety of foodstuffs for Celts and Britons. The Anglo-Saxons developed meat and savoury herb stewing techniques before the practice became common in Europe. The <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest of England</a> introduced exotic spices into Britain in the Middle Ages.<sup id="cite_ref-Spencer_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spencer-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The British Empire facilitated a knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Indian_cuisine" title="Indian cuisine">India\'s food tradition</a> of "strong, penetrating spices and herbs".<sup id="cite_ref-Spencer_198-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spencer-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rationing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rationing in the United Kingdom">Food rationing policies</a>, imposed by the British government during wartime periods of the 20th century, are said to have been the stimulus for British cuisine\'s poor international reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-Spencer_198-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spencer-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British dishes include <a href="/wiki/Fish_and_chips" title="Fish and chips">fish and chips</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sunday_roast" title="Sunday roast">Sunday roast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bangers_and_mash" title="Bangers and mash">bangers and mash</a>. British cuisine has several national and regional varieties, including <a href="/wiki/English_cuisine" title="English cuisine">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_cuisine" title="Scottish cuisine">Scottish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_cuisine" title="Welsh cuisine">Welsh cuisine</a>, each of which has developed its own regional or local dishes, many of which are <a href="/wiki/Geographically_indicated_foods_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Geographically indicated foods of the United Kingdom">geographically indicated foods</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Cheddar_cheese" title="Cheddar cheese">Cheddar cheese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheshire_cheese" title="Cheshire cheese">Cheshire cheese</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_pudding" title="Yorkshire pudding">Yorkshire pudding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arbroath_Smokie" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbroath Smokie">Arbroath Smokie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_pasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornish pasty">Cornish pasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_cake" title="Welsh cake">Welsh cakes</a>.\n</p><p>The British are the second largest per capita <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a> consumers in the world, consuming an average of 2.1 kilograms (4.6&#160;lb) per person each year.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_tea_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="British tea culture">British tea culture</a> dates back to the 19th century, when <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> was part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and British interests controlled tea production in the subcontinent.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_literature" title="British literature">British literature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Languages of the United Kingdom">Languages of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>There is no single British language, though <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is by far the main language spoken by British citizens, being spoken monolingually by more than 70% of the UK population. English is therefore the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> official language of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> However, under the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Gaelic">Irish Gaelic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manx_language" title="Manx language">Manx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a> and Lowland Scots languages are officially recognised as Regional or Minority languages by the UK Government.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_language" title="Indigenous language">indigenous languages</a> which continue to be spoken as a first language by native inhabitants, Welsh and Scottish Gaelic have a different legal status from other minority languages. In some parts of the UK, some of these languages are commonly spoken as a first language; in wider areas, their use in a bilingual context is sometimes supported and/or promoted by central and/or local government policy. For naturalisation purposes, a competence standard of English, Scottish Gaelic or Welsh is required to pass the <a href="/wiki/Life_in_the_United_Kingdom_test" title="Life in the United Kingdom test">life in the United Kingdom test</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> However, English is used routinely, and although considered culturally important, Scottish Gaelic and Welsh are much less used.\n</p><p>Throughout the United Kingdom there are distinctive spoken expressions and <a href="/wiki/Regional_accents_of_English" title="Regional accents of English">regional accents of English</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Rosen3_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rosen3-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> which are seen to be symptomatic of a locality\'s culture and identity.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> An awareness and knowledge of accents in the United Kingdom can "place, within a few miles, the locality in which a man or woman has grown up".<sup id="cite_ref-Rose54_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rose54-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=British_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_literature" title="British literature">British literature</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jk-rowling-crop.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Jk-rowling-crop.JPG/170px-Jk-rowling-crop.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Jk-rowling-crop.JPG/255px-Jk-rowling-crop.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Jk-rowling-crop.JPG 2x" data-file-width="297" data-file-height="446" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jk-rowling-crop.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/J.K._Rowling" class="mw-redirect" title="J.K. Rowling">J.K. Rowling</a> is one of the world\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_fiction_authors" title="List of best-selling fiction authors">best selling</a> British authors. Her <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></i> series of books have sold more than 400 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/British_literature" title="British literature">British literature</a> is "one of the leading literatures in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroichBassnett200127_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroichBassnett200127-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The overwhelming part is written in the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>, but there are also pieces of literature written in <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_literature" title="Cornish literature">Cornish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>.\n</p><p>Britain has a long history of famous and influential authors.
